# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\\n47: //\\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \\\"absent\\\".\\n52: //\\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\\n65: // selector.\\n66: //\\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\\n73: //\\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\\n75: // during `Run()`.\\n76: //\\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\\n84: //\\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\\n91: //\\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\\n96: // into its constituent parts.\\n97: //\\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\\n101: //\\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\\n127: //\\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\\n131: // to something else, for example through a\\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\\n133: //\\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\\n138: \\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\\n139: \\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\\n140: \\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\\n141: \\t// different handlers.\\n142: \\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\\n143: \\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\\n144: \\t// seen every item in the initial list).\\n145: \\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\\n146: \\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\\n147: \\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\\n148: \\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\\n149: \\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\\n150: \\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\\n151: \\t// any interactions with the authoritative storage. \\tresyncNeeded := false\\n832: \\tnow := p.clock.Now()\\n833: \\tfor listener := range p.listeners {\\n834: \\t\\t// need to loop through all the listeners to see if they need to resync so we can \\t}\\n856: }\\n857: \\n858: // processorListener relays notifications from a sharedProcessor to\\n859: // one ResourceEventHandler --- using two goroutines, two unbuffered\\n860: // channels, and an unbounded ring buffer.  The `add(notification)`\\n861: // function sends the given notification to `addCh`.  One goroutine\\n862: // runs `pop()`, which pumps notifications from `addCh` to `nextCh`\\n863: // using storage in the ring buffer while `nextCh` is not keeping up.\\n864: // Another goroutine runs `run()`, which receives notifications from\\n865: // `nextCh` and synchronously invokes the appropriate handler method.\\n866: //\\n867: // processorListener also keeps track of the adjusted requested resync\\n868: // period of the listener.\\n869: type processorListener struct {\\n870: \\tnextCh chan interface{}\\n871: \\taddCh  chan interface{}\\n872: \\n873: \\thandler ResourceEventHandler\\n874: \\n875: \\tsyncTracker *synctrack.SingleFileTracker\\n876: \\n877: \\t// pendingNotifications is an unbounded ring buffer that holds all notifications not yet distributed.\\n878: \\t// There is one per listener, but a failing/stalled listener will have infinite pendingNotifications\\n879: \\t// added until we OOM.\\n880: \\t// TODO: This is no worse than before, since reflectors were backed by unbounded DeltaFIFOs, but\\n881: \\t// we should try to do something better.\\n882: \\tpendingNotifications buffer.RingGrowing\\n883: \\n884: \\t// requestedResyncPeriod is how frequently the listener wants a\\n885: \\t// full resync from the shared informer, but modified by two\\n886: \\t// adjustments.  One is imposing a lower bound,\\n887: \\t// `minimumResyncPeriod`.  The other is another lower bound, the\\n888: \\t// sharedIndexInformer's `resyncCheckPeriod`, that is imposed (a) only\\n889: \\t// in AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod invocations made after the\\n890: \\t// sharedIndexInformer starts and (b) only if the informer does\\n891: \\t// resyncs at all.\\n892: \\trequestedResyncPeriod time.Duration\\n893: \\t// resyncPeriod is the threshold that will be used in the logic\\n894: \\t// for this listener.  This value differs from\\n895: \\t// requestedResyncPeriod only when the sharedIndexInformer does\\n896: \\t// not do resyncs, in which case the value here is zero.  The\\n897: \\t// actual time between resyncs depends on when the\\n898: \\t// sharedProcessor's `shouldResync` function is invoked and when\\n899: \\t// the sharedIndexInformer processes `Sync` type Delta objects.\\n900: \\tresyncPeriod time.Duration\\n901: \\t// nextResync is the earliest time the listener should get a full resync\\n902: \\tnextResync time.Time\\n903: \\t// resyncLock guards access to resyncPeriod and nextResync\\n904: \\tresyncLock sync.Mutex\\n905: }\\n906: \\n907: // HasSynced returns true if the source informer has synced, and all\\n908: // corresponding events have been delivered.\\n909: func (p *processorListener) HasSynced() bool {\\n910: \\treturn p.syncTracker.HasSynced()\\n911: }\\n912: \\n913: func newProcessListener(handler ResourceEventHandler, requestedResyncPeriod, resyncPeriod time.Duration, now time.Time, bufferSize int, hasSynced func() bool) *processorListener {\\n914: \\tret := &processorListener{\\n915: \\t\\tnextCh:                make(chan interface{}),\\n916: \\t\\taddCh:                 make(chan interface{}),\\n917: \\t\\thandler:               handler,\\n918: \\t\\tsyncTracker:           &synctrack.SingleFileTracker{UpstreamHasSynced: hasSynced},\\n919: \\t\\tpendingNotifications:  *buffer.NewRingGrowing(bufferSize),\\n920: \\t\\trequestedResyncPeriod: requestedResyncPeriod,\\n921: \\t\\tresyncPeriod:          resyncPeriod,\\n922: \\t}\\n923: \\n924: \\tret.determineNextResync(now)\\n925: \\n926: \\treturn ret\\n927: }\\n928: \\n929: func (p *processorListener) add(notification interface{}) {\\n930: \\tif a, ok := notification.(addNotification); ok && a.isInInitialList {\\n931: \\t\\tp.syncTracker.Start()\\n932: \\t}\\n933: \\tp.addCh <- notification\\n934: }\\n935: \\n936: func (p *processorListener) pop() {\\n937: \\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\\n938: \\tdefer close(p.nextCh) // Tell .run() to stop\\n939: \\n940: \\tvar nextCh chan<- interface{}\\n941: \\tvar notification interface{}\\n942: \\tfor {\\n943: \\t\\tselect {\\n944: \\t\\tcase nextCh <- notification:\\n945: \\t\\t\\t// Notification dispatched\\n946: \\t\\t\\tvar ok bool\\n947: \\t\\t\\tnotification, ok = p.pendingNotifications.ReadOne()\\n948: \\t\\t\\tif !ok { // Nothing to pop\\n949: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextCh = nil // Disable this select case\\n950: \\t\\t\\t}\\n951: \\t\\tcase notificationToAdd, ok := <-p.addCh:\\n952: \\t\\t\\tif !ok {\\n953: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n954: \\t\\t\\t}\\n955: \\t\\t\\tif notification == nil { // No notification to pop (and pendingNotifications is empty)\\n956: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Optimize the case - skip adding to pendingNotifications\\n957: \\t\\t\\t\\tnotification = notificationToAdd\\n958: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextCh = p.nextCh\\n959: \\t\\t\\t} else { // There is already a notification waiting to be dispatched\\n960: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.pendingNotifications.WriteOne(notificationToAdd)\\n961: \\t\\t\\t}\\n962: \\t\\t}\\n963: \\t}\\n964: }\\n965: \\n966: func (p *processorListener) run() {\\n967: \\t// this call blocks until the channel is closed.  When a panic happens during the notification\\n968: \\t// we will catch it, **the offending item will be skipped!**, and after a short delay (one second)\\n969: \\t// the next notification will be attempted.  This is usually better than the alternative of never\\n970: \\t// delivering again.\\n971: \\tstopCh := make(chan struct{})\\n972: \\twait.Until(func() {\\n973: \\t\\tfor next := range p.nextCh {\\n974: \\t\\t\\tswitch notification := next.(type) {\\n975: \\t\\t\\tcase updateNotification:\\n976: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnUpdate(notification.oldObj, notification.newObj)\\n977: \\t\\t\\tcase addNotification:\\n978: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnAdd(notification.newObj, notification.isInInitialList)\\n979: \\t\\t\\t\\tif notification.isInInitialList {\\n980: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tp.syncTracker.Finished()\\n981: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n982: \\t\\t\\tcase deleteNotification:\\n983: \\t\\t\\t\\tp.handler.OnDelete(notification.oldObj)\\n984: \\t\\t\\tdefault:\\n985: \\t\\t\\t\\tutilruntime.HandleError(fmt.Errorf(\\\"unrecognized notification: %T\\\", next))\\n986: \\t\\t\\t}\\n987: \\t\\t}\\n988: \\t\\t// the only way to get here is if the p.nextCh is empty and closed\\n989: \\t\\tclose(stopCh)\\n990: \\t}, 1*time.Second, stopCh)\\n991: }\\n992: \\n993: // shouldResync deterimines if the listener needs a resync. If the listener's resyncPeriod is 0,\\n994: // this always returns false.\\n995: func (p *processorListener) shouldResync(now time.Time) bool {\\n996: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n997: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n998: \\n999: \\tif p.resyncPeriod == 0 {\\n1000: \\t\\treturn false\\n1001: \\t}\\n1002: \\n1003: \\treturn now.After(p.nextResync) || now.Equal(p.nextResync)\\n1004: }\\n1005: \\n1006: func (p *processorListener) determineNextResync(now time.Time) {\\n1007: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n1008: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n1009: \\n1010: \\tp.nextResync = now.Add(p.resyncPeriod)\\n1011: }\\n1012: \\n1013: func (p *processorListener) setResyncPeriod(resyncPeriod time.Duration) {\\n1014: \\tp.resyncLock.Lock()\\n1015: \\tdefer p.resyncLock.Unlock()\\n1016: \\n1017: \\tp.resyncPeriod = resyncPeriod\\n1018: }\\n1019: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0@d17b464c6fcd3273e4b1f695890bf0af7d5b272d/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/shared_informer.go\"}",

    "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package cache\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"errors\"\n21: \t\"fmt\"\n22: \t\"sync\"\n23: \t\"time\"\n24: \n25: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n26: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n27: \tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n28: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n29: \t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n30: \t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n31: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n32: \n33: \t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n34: \n35: \tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n36: )\n37: \n38: // SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n39: // clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n40: // objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n41: // namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n42: // an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n43: // SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n44: // group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n45: // SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n46: // applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n47: //\n48: // The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n49: // access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n50: // An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n51: // other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n52: //\n53: // A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n54: // by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n55: // machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n56: // the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n57: // consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n58: // prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n59: // particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n60: // then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n61: // eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n62: // state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n63: // service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n64: // absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n65: // selector.\n66: //\n67: // For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n68: // states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n69: // states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n70: // might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n71: // states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n72: // ordering between states seen for different objects.\n73: //\n74: // The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n75: // during `Run()`.\n76: //\n77: // As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n78: // unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n79: // collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n80: // SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n81: // collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n82: // service ends, or communication problems between the two\n83: // persistently thwart achievement).\n84: //\n85: // As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n86: // non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n87: // removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n88: // removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n89: // too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n90: // problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n91: //\n92: // The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n93: // objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n94: // Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n95: // a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n96: // into its constituent parts.\n97: //\n98: // Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n99: // snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n100: // will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n101: //\n102: // A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n103: // update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n104: // added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n105: // stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n106: // after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n107: // additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n108: // client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n109: // local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n110: // SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n111: // update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n112: // update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n113: // corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n114: // and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n115: // For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n116: // delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n117: // object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n118: // `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n119: // that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n120: // `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n121: // and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n122: // created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n123: // rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n124: // need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n125: // field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n126: // notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n127: //\n128: // A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n129: // is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n130: // notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n131: // to something else, for example through a\n132: // `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n133: //\n134: // A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n135: // state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n136: // ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\n137: type SharedInformer interface {\n138: \t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n139: \t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n140: \t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n141: \t// different handlers.\n142: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n143: \t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n144: \t// seen every item in the initial list).\n145: \tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n146: \t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n147: \t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n148: \t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n149: \t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n150: \t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add\n151: \t// any interactions with the authoritative storage.  Some\n152: \t// informers do no resyncs at all, not even for handlers added\n153: \t// with a non-zero resyncPeriod.  For an informer that does\n154: \t// resyncs, and for each handler that requests resyncs, that\n155: \t// informer develops a nominal resync period that is no shorter\n156: \t// than the requested period but may be longer.  The actual time\n157: \t// between any two resyncs may be longer than the nominal period\n158: \t// because the implementation takes time to do work and there may\n159: \t// be competing load and scheduling noise.\n160: \t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to remove\n161: \t// the handler again and an error if the handler cannot be added.\n162: \tAddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod(handler ResourceEventHandler, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n163: \t// RemoveEventHandler removes a formerly added event handler given by\n164: \t// its registration handle.\n165: \t// This function is guaranteed to be idempotent, and thread-safe.\n166: \tRemoveEventHandler(handle ResourceEventHandlerRegistration) error\n167: \t// GetStore returns the informer's local cache as a Store.\n168: \tGetStore() Store\n169: \t// GetController is deprecated, it does nothing useful\n170: \tGetController() Controller\n171: \t// Run starts and runs the shared informer, returning after it stops.\n172: \t// The informer will be stopped when stopCh is closed.\n173: \tRun(stopCh <-chan struct{})\n174: \t// HasSynced returns true if the shared informer's store has been\n175: \t// informed by at least one full LIST of the authoritative state\n176: \t// of the informer's object collection.  This is unrelated to \"resync\".\n177: \t//\n178: \t// Note that this doesn't tell you if an individual handler is synced!!\n179: \t// For that, please call HasSynced on the handle returned by\n180: \t// AddEventHandler.\n181: \tHasSynced() bool\n182: \t// LastSyncResourceVersion is the resource version observed when last synced with the underlying\n183: \t// store. The value returned is not synchronized with access to the underlying store and is not\n184: \t// thread-safe.\n185: \tLastSyncResourceVersion() string\n186: \n187: \t// The WatchErrorHandler is called whenever ListAndWatch drops the\n188: \t// connection with an error. After calling this handler, the informer\n189: \t// will backoff and retry.\n190: \t//\n191: \t// The default implementation looks at the error type and tries to log\n192: \t// the error message at an appropriate level.\n193: \t//\n194: \t// There's only one handler, so if you call this multiple times, last one\n195: \t// wins; calling after the informer has been started returns an error.\n196: \t//\n197: \t// The handler is intended for visibility, not to e.g. pause the consumers.\n198: \t// The handler should return quickly - any expensive processing should be\n199: \t// offloaded.\n200: \tSetWatchErrorHandler(handler WatchErrorHandler) error\n201: \n202: \t// The TransformFunc is called for each object which is about to be stored.\n203: \t//\n204: \t// This function is intended for you to take the opportunity to\n205: \t// remove, transform, or normalize fields. One use case is to strip unused\n206: \t// metadata fields out of objects to save on RAM cost.\n207: \t//\n208: \t// Must be set before starting the informer.\n209: \t//\n210: \t// Please see the comment on TransformFunc for more details.\n211: \tSetTransform(handler TransformFunc) error\n212: \n213: \t// IsStopped reports whether the informer has already been stopped.\n214: \t// Adding event handlers to already stopped informers is not possible.\n215: \t// An informer already stopped will never be started again.\n216: \tIsStopped() bool\n217: }\n218: \n219: // Opaque interface representing the registration of ResourceEventHandler for\n220: // a SharedInformer. Must be supplied back to the same SharedInformer's\n221: // `RemoveEventHandler` to unregister the handlers.\n222: //\n223: // Also used to tell if the handler is synced (has had all items in the initial\n224: // list delivered).\n225: type ResourceEventHandlerRegistration interface {\n226: \t// HasSynced reports if both the parent has synced and all pre-sync\n227: \t// events have been delivered.\n228: \tHasSynced() bool\n229: }\n230: \n231: // SharedIndexInformer provides add and get Indexers ability based on SharedInformer.\n232: type SharedIndexInformer interface {\n233: \tSharedInformer\n234: \t// AddIndexers add indexers to the informer before it starts.\n235: \tAddIndexers(indexers Indexers) error\n236: \tGetIndexer() Indexer\n237: }\n238: \n239: // NewSharedInformer creates a new instance for the ListerWatcher. The other is to repeatedly Pop from the Queue\\n111: \\t// and process with the Config's ProcessFunc. call via go.\\n135: func (c *controller) Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) {\\n136: \\tdefer utilruntime.HandleCrash()\\n137: \\tgo func() {\\n138: \\t\\t<-stopCh\\n139: \\t\\tc.config.Queue.Close()\\n140: \\t}()\\n141: \\tr := NewReflectorWithOptions(\\n142: \\t\\tc.config.ListerWatcher,\\n143: \\t\\tc.config.ObjectType,\\n144: \\t\\tc.config.Queue,\\n145: \\t\\tReflectorOptions{\\n146: \\t\\t\\tResyncPeriod:    c.config.FullResyncPeriod,\\n147: \\t\\t\\tMinWatchTimeout: c.config.MinWatchTimeout,\\n148: \\t\\t\\tTypeDescription: c.config.ObjectDescription,\\n149: \\t\\t\\tClock:           c.clock,\\n150: \\t\\t},\\n151: \\t)\\n152: \\tr.ShouldResync = c.config.ShouldResync\\n153: \\tr.WatchListPageSize = c.config.WatchListPageSize\\n154: \\tif c.config.WatchErrorHandler != nil {\\n155: \\t\\tr.watchErrorHandler = c.config.WatchErrorHandler\\n156: \\t}\\n157: \\n158: \\tc.reflectorMutex.Lock()\\n159: \\tc.reflector = r\\n160: \\tc.reflectorMutex.Unlock()\\n161: \\n162: \\tvar wg wait.Group\\n163: \\n164: \\twg.StartWithChannel(stopCh, r.Run)\\n165: \\n166: \\twait.Until(c.processLoop, time.Second, stopCh)\\n167: \\twg.Wait()\\n168: }\\n169: \\n170: // Returns true once this controller has completed an initial resource listing\\n171: func (c *controller) HasSynced() bool {\\n172: \\treturn c.config.Queue.HasSynced()\\n173: }\\n174: \\n175: func (c *controller) LastSyncResourceVersion() string {\\n176: \\tc.reflectorMutex.RLock()\\n177: \\tdefer c.reflectorMutex.RUnlock()\\n178: \\tif c.reflector == nil {\\n179: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\"\\n180: \\t}\\n181: \\treturn c.reflector.LastSyncResourceVersion()\\n182: }\\n183: \\n184: // processLoop drains the work queue.\\n185: // TODO: Consider doing the processing in parallel. This will require a little thought\\n186: // to make sure that we don't end up processing the same object multiple times\\n187: // concurrently.\\n188: //\\n189: // TODO: Plumb through the stopCh here (and down to the queue) so that this can\\n190: // actually exit when the controller is stopped. Or just give up on this stuff\\n191: // ever being stoppable. Converting this whole package to use Context would\\n192: // also be helpful.\\n193: func (c *controller) processLoop() {\\n194: \\tfor {\\n195: \\t\\tobj, err := c.config.Queue.Pop(PopProcessFunc(c.config.Process))\\n196: \\t\\tif err != nil {\\n197: \\t\\t\\tif err == ErrFIFOClosed {\\n198: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n199: \\t\\t\\t}\\n200: \\t\\t\\tif c.config.RetryOnError {\\n201: \\t\\t\\t\\t// This is the safe way to re-enqueue.\\n202: \\t\\t\\t\\tc.config.Queue.AddIfNotPresent(obj)\\n203: \\t\\t\\t}\\n204: \\t\\t}\\n205: \\t}\\n206: }\\n207: \\n208: // ResourceEventHandler can handle notifications for events that\\n209: // happen to a resource. The events are informational only, so you\\n210: // can't return an error.  The handlers MUST NOT modify the objects\\n211: // received; this concerns not only the top level of structure but all\\n212: // the data structures reachable from it.\\n213: //   - OnAdd is called when an object is added.\\n214: //   - OnUpdate is called when an object is modified. Note that oldObj is the\\n215: //     last known state of the object-- it is possible that several changes\\n216: //     were combined together, so you can't use this to see every single\\n217: //     change. OnUpdate is also called when a re-list happens, and it will\\n218: //     get called even if nothing changed. This is useful for periodically\\n219: //     evaluating or syncing something.\\n220: //   - OnDelete will get the final state of the item if it is known, otherwise\\n221: //     it will get an object of type DeletedFinalStateUnknown. This can\\n222: //     happen if the watch is closed and misses the delete event and we don't\\n223: //     notice the deletion until the subsequent re-list.\\n224: type ResourceEventHandler interface {\\n225: \\tOnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\\n226: \\tOnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{})\\n227: \\tOnDelete(obj interface{})\\n228: }\\n229: \\n230: // ResourceEventHandlerFuncs is an adaptor to let you easily specify as many or\\n231: // as few of the notification functions as you want while still implementing\\n232: // ResourceEventHandler.  This adapter does not remove the prohibition against\\n233: // modifying the objects.\\n234: //\\n235: // See ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs if your use needs to propagate\\n236: // HasSynced.\\n237: type ResourceEventHandlerFuncs struct {\\n238: \\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{})\\n239: \\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\\n240: \\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\\n241: }\\n242: \\n243: // OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\\n244: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\\n245: \\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\\n246: \\t\\tr.AddFunc(obj)\\n247: \\t}\\n248: }\\n249: \\n250: // OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\\n251: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\\n252: \\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\\n253: \\t\\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\\n254: \\t}\\n255: }\\n256: \\n257: // OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\\n258: func (r ResourceEventHandlerFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\\n259: \\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\\n260: \\t\\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\\n261: \\t}\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs is exactly like ResourceEventHandlerFuncs\\n265: // except its AddFunc accepts the isInInitialList parameter, for propagating\\n266: // HasSynced.\\n267: type ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs struct {\\n268: \\tAddFunc    func(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool)\\n269: \\tUpdateFunc func(oldObj, newObj interface{})\\n270: \\tDeleteFunc func(obj interface{})\\n271: }\\n272: \\n273: // OnAdd calls AddFunc if it's not nil.\\n274: func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\\n275: \\tif r.AddFunc != nil {\\n276: \\t\\tr.AddFunc(obj, isInInitialList)\\n277: \\t}\\n278: }\\n279: \\n280: // OnUpdate calls UpdateFunc if it's not nil.\\n281: func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\\n282: \\tif r.UpdateFunc != nil {\\n283: \\t\\tr.UpdateFunc(oldObj, newObj)\\n284: \\t}\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: // OnDelete calls DeleteFunc if it's not nil.\\n288: func (r ResourceEventHandlerDetailedFuncs) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\\n289: \\tif r.DeleteFunc != nil {\\n290: \\t\\tr.DeleteFunc(obj)\\n291: \\t}\\n292: }\\n293: \\n294: // FilteringResourceEventHandler applies the provided filter to all events coming\\n295: // in, ensuring the appropriate nested handler method is invoked. An object\\n296: // that starts passing the filter after an update is considered an add, and an\\n297: // object that stops passing the filter after an update is considered a delete.\\n298: // Like the handlers, the filter MUST NOT modify the objects it is given.\\n299: type FilteringResourceEventHandler struct {\\n300: \\tFilterFunc func(obj interface{}) bool\\n301: \\tHandler    ResourceEventHandler\\n302: }\\n303: \\n304: // OnAdd calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\\n305: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnAdd(obj interface{}, isInInitialList bool) {\\n306: \\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\\n307: \\t\\treturn\\n308: \\t}\\n309: \\tr.Handler.OnAdd(obj, isInInitialList)\\n310: }\\n311: \\n312: // OnUpdate ensures the proper handler is called depending on whether the filter matches\\n313: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj interface{}) {\\n314: \\tnewer := r.FilterFunc(newObj)\\n315: \\tolder := r.FilterFunc(oldObj)\\n316: \\tswitch {\\n317: \\tcase newer && older:\\n318: \\t\\tr.Handler.OnUpdate(oldObj, newObj)\\n319: \\tcase newer && !older:\\n320: \\t\\tr.Handler.OnAdd(newObj, false)\\n321: \\tcase !newer && older:\\n322: \\t\\tr.Handler.OnDelete(oldObj)\\n323: \\tdefault:\\n324: \\t\\t// do nothing\\n325: \\t}\\n326: }\\n327: \\n328: // OnDelete calls the nested handler only if the filter succeeds\\n329: func (r FilteringResourceEventHandler) OnDelete(obj interface{}) {\\n330: \\tif !r.FilterFunc(obj) {\\n331: \\t\\treturn\\n332: \\t}\\n333: \\tr.Handler.OnDelete(obj)\\n334: }\\n335: \\n336: // DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc checks for\\n337: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\\n338: // MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\\n339: func DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj interface{}) (string, error) {\\n340: \\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\\n341: \\t\\treturn d.Key, nil\\n342: \\t}\\n343: \\treturn MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)\\n344: }\\n345: \\n346: // DeletionHandlingObjectToName checks for\\n347: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown objects before calling\\n348: // ObjectToName.\\n349: func DeletionHandlingObjectToName(obj interface{}) (ObjectName, error) {\\n350: \\tif d, ok := obj.(DeletedFinalStateUnknown); ok {\\n351: \\t\\treturn ParseObjectName(d.Key)\\n352: \\t}\\n353: \\treturn ObjectToName(obj)\\n354: }\\n355: \\n356: // InformerOptions configure a Reflector.\\n357: type InformerOptions struct {\\n358: \\t// ListerWatcher implements List and Watch functions for the source of the resource\\n359: \\t// the informer will be informing about.\\n360: \\tListerWatcher ListerWatcher\\n361: \\n362: \\t// ObjectType is an object of the type that informer is expected to receive.\\n363: \\tObjectType runtime.Object\\n364: \\n365: \\t// Handler defines functions that should called on object mutations.\\n366: \\tHandler ResourceEventHandler\\n367: \\n368: \\t// ResyncPeriod is the underlying Reflector's resync period. If non-zero, the store\\n369: \\t// is re-synced with that frequency - Modify events are delivered even if objects\\n370: \\t// didn't change.\\n371: \\t// This is useful for synchronizing objects that configure external resources\\n372: \\t// (e.g. configure cloud provider functionalities).\\n373: \\t// Optional - if unset, store resyncing is not happening periodically.\\n374: \\tResyncPeriod time.Duration\\n375: \\n376: \\t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\\n377: \\t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\\n378: \\t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\\n379: \\t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\\n380: \\tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\\n381: \\n382: \\t// Indexers, if set, are the indexers for the received objects to optimize\\n383: \\t// certain queries.\\n384: \\t// Optional - if unset no indexes are maintained.\\n385: \\tIndexers Indexers\\n386: \\n387: \\t// Transform function, if set, will be called on all objects before they will be\\n388: \\t// put into the Store and corresponding Add/Modify/Delete handlers will be invoked\\n389: \\t// for them.\\n390: \\t// Optional - if unset no additional transforming is happening.\\n391: \\tTransform TransformFunc\\n392: }\\n393: \\n394: // NewInformerWithOptions returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\\n395: // while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\\n396: // Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\\n397: // notifications to be faulty.\\n398: func NewInformerWithOptions(options InformerOptions) (Store, Controller) {\\n399: \\tvar clientState Store\\n400: \\tif options.Indexers == nil {\\n401: \\t\\tclientState = NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\\n402: \\t} else {\\n403: \\t\\tclientState = NewIndexer(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc, options.Indexers)\\n404: \\t}\\n405: \\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\\n406: }\\n407: \\n408: // NewInformer returns a Store and a controller for populating the store\\n409: // while also providing event notifications. You should only used the returned\\n410: // Store for Get/List operations; Add/Modify/Deletes will cause the event\\n411: // notifications to be faulty.\\n412: //\\n413: // Parameters:\\n414: //   - lw is list and watch functions for the source of the resource you want to\\n415: //     be informed of.\\n416: //   - objType is an object of the type that you expect to receive.\\n417: //   - resyncPeriod: if non-zero, will re-list this often (you will get OnUpdate\\n418: //     calls, even if nothing changed). Otherwise, re-list will be delayed as\\n419: //     long as possible (until the upstream source closes the watch or times out,\\n420: //     or you stop the controller).\\n421: //   - h is the object you want notifications sent to.\\n422: //\\n423: // Deprecated: Use NewInformerWithOptions instead.\\n424: func NewInformer(\\n425: \\tlw ListerWatcher,\\n426: \\tobjType runtime.Object,\\n427: \\tresyncPeriod time.Duration,\\n428: \\th ResourceEventHandler,\\n429: ) (Store, Controller) {\\n430: \\t// This will hold the client state, as we know it.\\n431: \\tclientState := NewStore(DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc)\\n432: \\n433: \\toptions := InformerOptions{\\n434: \\t\\tListerWatcher: lw,\\n435: \\t\\tObjectType:    objType,\\n436: \\t\\tHandler:       h,\\n437: \\t\\tResyncPeriod:  resyncPeriod,\\n438: \\t}\\n439: \\treturn clientState, newInformer(clientState, options)\\n440: }\\n441: \\n442: // NewIndexerInformer returns an Indexer and a Controller for populating the index\\n443: // while also providing event notifications.     "content": "1: /*\n2: Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n3: \n4: Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n5: you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n6: You may obtain a copy of the License at\n7: \n8:     http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n9: \n10: Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n11: distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n12: WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n13: See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n14: limitations under the License.\n15: */\n16: \n17: package cache\n18: \n19: import (\n20: \t\"errors\"\n21: \t\"sync\"\n22: \t\"time\"\n23: \n24: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n25: \tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n26: \t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n27: \t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n28: )\n29: \n30: // This file implements a low-level controller that is used in\n31: // sharedIndexInformer, which is an implementation of\n32: // SharedIndexInformer.  Such informers, in turn, are key components\n33: // in the high level controllers that form the backbone of the\n34: // Kubernetes control plane.  Look at those for examples, or the\n35: // example in\n36: // https://github.com/kubernetes/client-go/tree/master/examples/workqueue\n37: // .\n38: \n39: // Config contains all the settings for one of these low-level controllers.\n40: type Config struct {\n41: \t// The queue for your objects - has to be a DeltaFIFO due to\n42: \t// assumptions in the implementation. Your Process() function\n43: \t// should accept the output of this Queue's Pop() method.\n44: \tQueue\n45: \n46: \t// Something that can list and watch your objects.\n47: \tListerWatcher\n48: \n49: \t// Something that can process a popped Deltas.\n50: \tProcess ProcessFunc\n51: \n52: \t// ObjectType is an example object of the type this controller is\n53: \t// expected to handle.\n54: \tObjectType runtime.Object\n55: \n56: \t// ObjectDescription is the description to use when logging type-specific information about this controller.\n57: \tObjectDescription string\n58: \n59: \t// FullResyncPeriod is the period at which ShouldResync is considered.\n60: \tFullResyncPeriod time.Duration\n61: \n62: \t// MinWatchTimeout, if set, will define the minimum timeout for watch requests send\n63: \t// to kube-apiserver. However, values lower than 5m will not be honored to avoid\n64: \t// negative performance impact on controlplane.\n65: \t// Optional - if unset a default value of 5m will be used.\n66: \tMinWatchTimeout time.Duration\n67: \n68: \t// ShouldResync is periodically used by the reflector to determine\n69: \t// whether to Resync the Queue. If ShouldResync is `nil` or\n70: \t// returns true, it means the reflector should proceed with the\n71: \t// resync.\n72: \tShouldResync ShouldResyncFunc\n73: \n74: \t// If true, when Process() returns an error, re-enqueue the object.\n75: \t// TODO: add interface to let you inject a delay/backoff or drop\n76: \t//       the object completely if desired. nil\\n606: }\\n607: \\n608: // watchList establishes a stream to get a consistent snapshot of data\\n609: // from the server as described in https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/3157-watch-list#proposal\\n610: //\\n611: // case 1: start at Most Recent (RV=\\\"\\\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\\n612: // Establishes a consistent stream with the server.\\n613: // That means the returned data is consistent, as if, served directly from etcd via a quorum read.\\n614: // It begins with synthetic \\\"Added\\\" events of all resources up to the most recent ResourceVersion.\\n615: // It ends with a synthetic \\\"Bookmark\\\" event containing the most recent ResourceVersion.\\n616: // After receiving a \\\"Bookmark\\\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\\n617: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\\n618: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\\n619: //\\n620: // case 2: start at Exact (RV>\\\"0\\\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\\n621: // synthetic \\\"Bookmark\\\" event containing the provided or newer resource version.\\n624: // After receiving a \\\"Bookmark\\\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\\n625: // It It should be used carefully as paginated lists are always served directly from\n104: \t// etcd, which is significantly less efficient and may lead to serious performance and\n105: \t// scalability problems.\n106: \tWatchListPageSize int64\n107: \t// ShouldResync is invoked periodically and whenever it returns `true` the Store's Resync operation is invoked\n108: \tShouldResync func() bool\n109: \t// MaxInternalErrorRetryDuration defines how long we should retry internal errors returned by watch.\n110: \tMaxInternalErrorRetryDuration time.Duration\n111: \t// UseWatchList if turned on instructs the reflector to open a stream to bring data from the API server.\n112: \t// Streaming has the primary advantage of using fewer server's resources to fetch data.\n113: \t//\n114: \t// The old behaviour establishes a LIST request which gets data in chunks.\n115: \t// Paginated list is less efficient and depending on the actual size of objects\n116: \t// might result in an increased memory consumption of the APIServer.\n117: \t//\n118: \t// See https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/3157-watch-list#design-details\n119: \t//\n120: \t// TODO(#115478): Consider making reflector.UseWatchList a private field. Since we implemented \"api streaming\" on the etcd storage layer it should work.\n121: \tUseWatchList *bool\n122: }\n123: \n124: func (r *Reflector) Name() string {\n125: \treturn r.name\n126: }\n127: \n128: func (r *Reflector) TypeDescription() string {\n129: \treturn r.typeDescription\n130: }\n131: \n132: // ResourceVersionUpdater is an interface that allows store implementation to\n133: // track the current resource version of the reflector. This is especially\n134: // important if storage bookmarks are enabled.\n135: type ResourceVersionUpdater interface {\n136: \t// UpdateResourceVersion is called each time current resource version of the reflector\n137: \t// is updated.\n138: \tUpdateResourceVersion(resourceVersion string)\n139: }\n140: \n141: // The WatchErrorHandler is called whenever ListAndWatch drops the\n142: // connection with an error. After calling this handler, the informer\n143: // will backoff and retry.\n144: //\n145: // The default implementation looks at the error type and tries to log\n146: // the error message at an appropriate level.\n147: //\n148: // Implementations of this handler may display the error message in other\n149: // ways. Implementations should return quickly - any expensive processing\n150: // should be offloaded.\n151: type WatchErrorHandler func(r *Reflector, err error)\n152: \n153: // DefaultWatchErrorHandler is the default implementation of WatchErrorHandler\n154: func DefaultWatchErrorHandler(r *Reflector, err error) {\n155: \tswitch {\n156: \tcase isExpiredError(err):\n157: \t\t// Don't set LastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable - LIST call with ResourceVersion=RV already\n158: \t\t// has a semantic that it returns data at least as fresh as provided RV.\n159: \t\t// So first try to LIST with setting RV to resource version of last observed object.\n160: \t\tklog.V(4).Infof(\"%s: watch of %v closed with: %v\", r.name, r.typeDescription, err)\n161: \tcase err == io.EOF:\n162: \t\t// watch closed normally\n163: \tcase err == io.ErrUnexpectedEOF:\n164: \t\tklog.V(1).Infof(\"%s: Watch for %v closed with unexpected EOF: %v\", r.name, r.typeDescription, err)\n165: \tdefault:\n166: \t\tutilruntime.HandleError(fmt.Errorf(\"%s: Failed to watch %v: %v\", r.name, r.typeDescription, err))\n167: \t}\n168: }\n169: \n170: // NewNamespaceKeyedIndexerAndReflector creates an Indexer and a Reflector\n171: // The indexer is configured to key on namespace\n172: func NewNamespaceKeyedIndexerAndReflector(lw ListerWatcher, expectedType interface{}, resyncPeriod time.Duration) (indexer Indexer, reflector *Reflector) {\n173: \tindexer = NewIndexer(MetaNamespaceKeyFunc, Indexers{NamespaceIndex: MetaNamespaceIndexFunc})\n174: \treflector = NewReflector(lw, expectedType, indexer, resyncPeriod)\n175: \treturn indexer, reflector\n176: }\n177: \n178: // NewReflector creates a new Reflector with its name defaulted to the closest source_file.go:line in the call stack\n179: // that is outside this package. If unset defaults to clock.RealClock{}\n212: \tClock clock.Clock\n213: }\n214: \n215: // NewReflectorWithOptions creates a new Reflector object which will keep the\n216: // given store up to date with the server's contents for the given\n217: // resource. If\n219: // resyncPeriod is non-zero, then the reflector will periodically\n220: // consult its ShouldResync function to determine whether to invoke\n221: // the Store's Resync operation; `ShouldResync==nil` means always\n222: // \"yes\".  This enables you to use reflectors to periodically process\n223: // everything as well as incrementally processing the things that\n224: // change.\n225: func NewReflectorWithOptions(lw ListerWatcher, expectedType interface{}, store Store, options ReflectorOptions) *Reflector {\n226: \treflectorClock := options.Clock\n227: \tif reflectorClock == nil {\n228: \t\treflectorClock = clock.RealClock{}\n229: \t}\n230: \tminWatchTimeout := defaultMinWatchTimeout\n231: \tif options.MinWatchTimeout > defaultMinWatchTimeout {\n232: \t\tminWatchTimeout = options.MinWatchTimeout\n233: \t}\n234: \tr := &Reflector{\n235: \t\tname:            options.Name,\n236: \t\tresyncPeriod:    options.ResyncPeriod,\n237: \t\tminWatchTimeout: minWatchTimeout,\n238: \t\ttypeDescription: options.TypeDescription,\n239: \t\tlisterWatcher:   lw,\n240: \t\tstore:           store,\n241: \t\t// We used to make the call every 1sec (1 QPS), the goal here is to achieve ~98% traffic reduction when\n242: \t\t// API server is not healthy. With these parameters, backoff will stop at [30,60) sec interval which is\n243: \t\t// 0.22 QPS. If we don't backoff for 2min, assume API server is healthy and we reset the backoff.\n244: \t\tbackoffManager:    wait.NewExponentialBackoffManager(800*time.Millisecond, 30*time.Second, 2*time.Minute, 2.0, 1.0, reflectorClock),\n245: \t\tclock:             reflectorClock,\n246: \t\twatchErrorHandler: WatchErrorHandler(DefaultWatchErrorHandler),\n247: \t\texpectedType:      reflect.TypeOf(expectedType),\n248: \t}\n249: \n250: \tif r.name == \"\" {\n251: \t\tr.name = naming.GetNameFromCallsite(internalPackages...)\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \tif r.typeDescription == \"\" \t}\n261: \n262: \t// don't overwrite UseWatchList if already set\n263: \t// because the higher layers (e.g. storage/cacher) disabled it on purpose\n264: \tif r.UseWatchList == nil {\n265: }\n344: \n345: // ListAndWatch first lists all items and get the resource version at the moment of call,\n346: // and then use the resource version to watch.\n347: // It returns error if ListAndWatch didn't even try to initialize watch.\n348: func (r *Reflector) ListAndWatch(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n349: \tklog.V(3).Infof(\"Listing and watching %v from %s\", r.typeDescription, server at the moment of the call.\n501: // the resource version can be used for further progress notification (aka. watch).\n502: func (r *Reflector) list(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error {\n503: \tvar Assume this resource and server honor\n529: \t\t\t// paging requests (i.e. watch cache is probably disabled) and leave the default\n530: \t\t\t// pager size set.\n531: \t\tcase options.ResourceVersion != \"\" && options.ResourceVersion != \"0\":\n532: \t\t\t// User didn't explicitly request pagination.\n533: \t\t\t//\n534: \t\t\t// With ResourceVersion != \"\", we have a possibility to list from watch cache,\n535: \t\t\t// but we do that (for ResourceVersion != \"0\") only if Limit is unset.\n536: \t\t\t// To avoid thundering herd on etcd (e.g. on master upgrades), we explicitly\n537: \t\t\t// switch off pagination to force listing from watch cache (if enabled).\n538: \t\t\t// With the existing semantic of RV (result is at least as fresh as provided RV),\n539: \t\t\t// this is correct and doesn't lead to going back in time.\n540: \t\t\t//\n541: \t\t\t// We also don't turn off pagination for ResourceVersion=\"0\", since watch cache\n542: \t\t\t// is ignoring Limit in that case anyway, and if watch cache is not enabled\n543: \t\t\t// we don't introduce regression.\n544: \t\t\tpager.PageSize = 0\n545: \t\t}\n546: \n547: \t\tlist, paginatedResult, err = pager.ListWithAlloc(context.Background(), options)\n548: \t\tif isExpiredError(err) || isTooLargeResourceVersionError(err) {\n549: \t\t\tr.setIsLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable(true)\n550: \t\t\t// Retry immediately if the resource version used to list is unavailable.\n551: \t\t\t// The pager already falls back to full list if paginated list calls fail due to an \"Expired\" error on\n552: \t\t\t// continuation pages, but the pager might not be enabled, the full list might fail because the\n553: \t\t\t// resource version it is listing at is expired or the cache may not yet be synced to the provided\n554: \t\t\t// resource version. The reasoning behind it is that later, in some\n576: \t// situations we may force listing directly from etcd (by setting ResourceVersion=\"\")\n577: \t// which will return paginated result, even if watch cache is enabled. However, in\n578: \t// that case, we still want to prefer sending requests to watch cache if possible.\n579: \t//\n580: \t// Paginated result returned for request with ResourceVersion=\"0\" mean that watch\n581: \t// cache is disabled and there are a lot of objects of a given type. \tr.setIsLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable(false) // list was successful\n588: \tlistMetaInterface, err := meta.ListAccessor(list)\n589: \tif err != nil {\n590: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"unable to consistent snapshot of data\n609: // from the server as described in https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/tree/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/3157-watch-list#proposal\n610: //\n611: // case 1: start at Most Recent (RV=\"\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\n612: // Establishes a consistent stream with the server.\n613: // That means the returned data is consistent, as if, served directly from etcd via a quorum read.\n614: // It begins with synthetic \"Added\" events of all resources up to the most recent ResourceVersion.\n615: // It ends with a synthetic \"Bookmark\" event containing the most recent ResourceVersion.\n616: // After receiving a \"Bookmark\" event the reflector is considered to be synchronized.\n617: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\n618: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\n619: //\n620: // case 2: start at Exact (RV>\"0\", ResourceVersionMatch=ResourceVersionMatchNotOlderThan)\n621: // Establishes a stream with the server at the provided resource version.\n622: // To establish the initial state the server begins with considered to be synchronized.\n625: // It replaces its internal store with the collected items and\n626: // reuses the current watch requests for getting further events.\n627: func (r *Reflector) One is that the\\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\\n69: //\\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\\n74: // resync events.\\n75: //\\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\\n78: // the Pop() method.\\n79: //\\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\\n86: //\\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. All are\n32: // optional.\n33: type DeltaFIFOOptions struct {\n34: \n35: \t// KeyFunction is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It's\n36: \t// exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional\n37: \t// handling around deleted objects and queue state).\n38: \t// Optional, the default is MetaNamespaceKeyFunc.\n39: \tKeyFunction KeyFunc\n40: \n41: \t// KnownObjects is expected to return a list of keys that the consumer of\n42: \t// this queue \"knows about\". It is used to decide which items are missing\n43: \t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n44: \t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n45: \tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n46: \n47: \t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n48: \t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Before the `Replaced` event type was\n49: \t// added, calls to Replace() were handled the same as Sync(). For\n50: \t// backwards-compatibility purposes, this is false by default.\n51: \t// When true, `Replaced` events will be sent for items passed to a Replace() call.\n52: \t// When false, `Sync` events will be sent instead.\n53: \tEmitDeltaTypeReplaced bool\n54: \n55: \t// If set, will be called for objects before enqueueing them. Please\n56: \t// see the comment on TransformFunc for details.\n57: \tTransformer TransformFunc\n58: }\n59: \n60: // DeltaFIFO is like FIFO, but differs in two ways.  One is that the\n61: // accumulator associated with a given object's key is not that object\n62: // but rather a Deltas, which is a slice of Delta values for that\n63: // object.  Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n64: // except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n65: // Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n66: // not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n67: // Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n68: // DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n69: //\n70: // The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n71: // an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n72: // If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n73: // replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n74: // resync events.\n75: //\n76: // DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n77: // intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n78: // the Pop() method.\n79: //\n80: // DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n81: //   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n82: //   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n83: //     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n84: //   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n85: //   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n86: //\n87: // DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n88: // interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n89: // will always return an object of type Deltas. List() returns\n90: // the newest object from each accumulator in the FIFO.\n91: //\n92: // A DeltaFIFO's knownObjects KeyListerGetter provides the abilities\n93: // to list Store keys and to get objects by Store key.  The objects in\n94: // question are called \"known objects\" and this set of objects\n95: // modifies the behavior of the Delete, Replace, and Resync methods\n96: // (each in a different way).\n97: //\n98: // A note on threading: If you call Pop() in parallel from multiple\n99: // threads, you could end up with multiple threads processing slightly\n100: // different versions of the same object.\n101: type DeltaFIFO struct {\n102: \t// lock/cond protects access to 'items' and 'queue'.\n103: \tlock sync.RWMutex\n104: \tcond sync.Cond\n105: \n106: \t// `items` maps a key to a Deltas.\n107: \t// Each such Deltas has at least one Delta.\n108: \titems map[string]Deltas\n109: \n110: \t// `queue` maintains FIFO order of keys for consumption in Pop().\n111: \t// There are no duplicates in `queue`.\n112: \t// A key is in `queue` if and only if it is in `items`.\n113: \tqueue []string\n114: \n115: \t// populated is true if the first batch of items inserted by Replace() has non-nil.\n138: \ttransformer TransformFunc\n139: }\n140: \n141: // TransformFunc allows for transforming an object before it will be processed.\n142: //\n143: // The most common usage pattern is to clean-up some parts of the object to\n144: // reduce component memory usage if a given component doesn't care about them.\n145: //\n146: // New in v1.27: TransformFunc sees the object before any other actor, and it\n147: // is now safe to mutate the object in place instead of making a copy.\n148: //\n149: // It's recommended for the TransformFunc to be idempotent.\n150: // It MUST be idempotent if objects already present in the cache are passed to\n151: // the Replace() to avoid re-mutating them. Default informers do not pass\n152: // existing objects to Replace though.\n153: //\n154: // Note that TransformFunc is called while inserting objects into the\n155: // notification queue and is therefore extremely performance sensitive; please\n156: // do not do anything that will take a long time.\n157: type TransformFunc func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)\n158: \n159: // DeltaType is the type of a change (addition, deletion, etc)\n160: type DeltaType string\n161: \n162: // Change type definition\n163: const (\n164: \tAdded   DeltaType = \"Added\"\n165: \tUpdated DeltaType = \"Updated\"\n166: \tDeleted DeltaType = \"Deleted\"\n167: \t// Replaced is emitted when we encountered watch errors and had to do a\n168: \t// relist. It tells you what\n180: // change happened, and the object's state after* that change.\n181: //\n182: // [*] Unless the change is a deletion, and then you'll get the final\n183: // state of the object before it was deleted.\n184: type Delta struct {\n185: \tType   DeltaType\n186: \tObject interface{}\n187: }\n188: \n189: // Deltas is a list of one or more 'Delta's to an individual object.\n190: // The oldest delta is at index 0, the newest delta is the last one.\n191: type Deltas []Delta\n192: \n193: // NewDeltaFIFO returns a Queue which can be used to process changes to items.\n194: //\n195: // keyFunc is used to figure out what key an object should have. (It is\n196: // exposed in the returned DeltaFIFO's KeyOf() method, with additional handling\n197: // around deleted objects and queue state).\n198: //\n199: // 'knownObjects' may be supplied to modify the behavior of Delete,\n200: // Replace, and Resync. Have to think about how that\n205: // affects error retrying.\n206: //\n207: //\tNOTE: It is possible to misuse this and cause a race when using an\n208: //\texternal known object source.\n209: //\tWhether there is a potential race depends on how the consumer\n210: //\tmodifies knownObjects. An `Indexer` for the local cache (allows efficient lookups)\\n2. A `Controller` that manages the reflector and processes queue items\\n3. A `sharedProcessor` that distributes notifications to registered event handlers\\n\\n## List-Watch Mechanism\\nThe list-watch pattern is implemented across two key files:\\n\\n### ListerWatcher Interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go`)\\nDefines the minimal interface for initial list and watch operations. The `ListWatch` struct provides concrete implementation with `NewListWatchFromClient()` factory that creates a ListerWatcher by binding to a Kubernetes REST client.\\n\\n### Reflector (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go`)\\nThe Reflector is the producer component that:\\n- Performs initial LIST operations to populate the cache with all existing objects\\n- Establishes a WATCH connection to receive real-time updates\\n- Implements exponential backoff for connection failures\\n- Periodically issues full LIST operations (resyncs) to detect missed updates\\n- Pushes all changes into the DeltaFIFO queue\\n- Provides `LastSyncResourceVersion()` to track the API server state\\n\\n## Local Cache Store Sync\\nThe local cache is implemented through a layered approach in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`:\\n\\n### Store (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go`)\\nBasic key-value store interface and implementation:\\n- `NewStore()` creates a simple cache backed by a ThreadSafeStore\\n- Supports Add, Update, Delete, Get, List operations\\n- Uses `DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc` as key function (namespace/name format)\\n\\n### Indexer (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go`)\\nExtends Store with indexing capability:\\n- `NewIndexer()` wraps ThreadSafeStore with configurable index functions\\n- Allows efficient filtering by field or label selectors\\n- Maintains multiple indices for complex queries\\n\\n### ThreadSafeStore (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\\nUnderlying thread-safe storage:\\n- Protects all cache operations with RWMutex locks\\n- Maintains both item storage and multiple indices\\n- Implements atomic updates\\n\\n## Control Loop and Delta Processing\\nThe `Controller` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go` (lines 96-206) orchestrates the flow:\\n1. Creates a Reflector with the ListerWatcher\\n2. Runs Reflector in a goroutine to feed the DeltaFIFO queue\\n3. `processLoop()` continuously pops items from the DeltaFIFO and processes them\\n4. `processDeltas()` updates the local cache and invokes registered handlers\\n\\n## Delta FIFO Queue\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (lines 60-178) is the critical queue implementation:\\n- Tracks changes as `Deltas` - sequences of state changes (Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, Replaced)\\n- Deduplicates consecutive identical operations\\n- Maintains FIFO ordering for processing\\n- Integrates with the local cache (\\\"knownObjects\\\") to generate synthetic Deleted deltas when objects disappear\\n- Supports periodic resync operations to detect missed updates\\n- Pop() operations are blocking, allowing the consumer to process one item at a time\\n\\n## Event Distribution\\nOnce items are processed by the controller and the local cache is updated, the `sharedProcessor` and `processorListener` components (in shared_informer.go, lines 705-991) distribute notifications to event handlers:\\n- Multiple event handlers can be registered on a single informer\\n- Handlers receive OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete callbacks\\n- Notifications include an `isInInitialList` flag to distinguish initial sync from live updates\\n- A ring buffer prevents slow handlers from blocking others\\n- Resync events periodically replay all cached objects to handlers that request them\\n\\n## Synchronization and Starting\\nThe `Start()` method in the factory (lines 143-165) initiates the entire pipeline:\\n1. Starts all registered informers in parallel goroutines\\n2. Each informer's Run() method starts its controller\\n3. The controller starts the reflector and begins the process loop\\n4. `WaitForCacheSync()` polls all informers' `HasSynced()` methods until they return true\\n5. Once synced, the local cache contains all objects from the API server\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that all components in Kubernetes that need to watch API resources can efficiently maintain a local cache in sync with the API server, with minimal network overhead and strong consistency guarantees.\"\n}\n",

An `Indexer` for the local cache (allows efficient lookups)\\n2. A `Controller` that manages the reflector and processes queue items\\n3. A `sharedProcessor` that distributes notifications to registered event handlers\\n\\n## List-Watch Mechanism\\nThe list-watch pattern is implemented across two key files:\\n\\n### ListerWatcher Interface (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/listwatch.go`)\\nDefines the minimal interface for initial list and watch operations. The `ListWatch` struct provides concrete implementation with `NewListWatchFromClient()` factory that creates a ListerWatcher by binding to a Kubernetes REST client.\\n\\n### Reflector (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/reflector.go`)\\nThe Reflector is the producer component that:\\n- Performs initial LIST operations to populate the cache with all existing objects\\n- Establishes a WATCH connection to receive real-time updates\\n- Implements exponential backoff for connection failures\\n- Periodically issues full LIST operations (resyncs) to detect missed updates\\n- Pushes all changes into the DeltaFIFO queue\\n- Provides `LastSyncResourceVersion()` to track the API server state\\n\\n## Local Cache Store Sync\\nThe local cache is implemented through a layered approach in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/`:\\n\\n### Store (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/store.go`)\\nBasic key-value store interface and implementation:\\n- `NewStore()` creates a simple cache backed by a ThreadSafeStore\\n- Supports Add, Update, Delete, Get, List operations\\n- Uses `DeletionHandlingMetaNamespaceKeyFunc` as key function (namespace/name format)\\n\\n### Indexer (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/index.go`)\\nExtends Store with indexing capability:\\n- `NewIndexer()` wraps ThreadSafeStore with configurable index functions\\n- Allows efficient filtering by field or label selectors\\n- Maintains multiple indices for complex queries\\n\\n### ThreadSafeStore (`staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`)\\nUnderlying thread-safe storage:\\n- Protects all cache operations with RWMutex locks\\n- Maintains both item storage and multiple indices\\n- Implements atomic updates\\n\\n## Control Loop and Delta Processing\\nThe `Controller` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/controller.go` (lines 96-206) orchestrates the flow:\\n1. Creates a Reflector with the ListerWatcher\\n2. Runs Reflector in a goroutine to feed the DeltaFIFO queue\\n3. `processLoop()` continuously pops items from the DeltaFIFO and processes them\\n4. `processDeltas()` updates the local cache and invokes registered handlers\\n\\n## Delta FIFO Queue\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (lines 60-178) is the critical queue implementation:\\n- Tracks changes as `Deltas` - sequences of state changes (Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, Replaced)\\n- Deduplicates consecutive identical operations\\n- Maintains FIFO ordering for processing\\n- Integrates with the local cache (\\\"knownObjects\\\") to generate synthetic Deleted deltas when objects disappear\\n- Supports periodic resync operations to detect missed updates\\n- Pop() operations are blocking, allowing the consumer to process one item at a time\\n\\n## Event Distribution\\nOnce items are processed by the controller and the local cache is updated, the `sharedProcessor` and `processorListener` components (in shared_informer.go, lines 705-991) distribute notifications to event handlers:\\n- Multiple event handlers can be registered on a single informer\\n- Handlers receive OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete callbacks\\n- Notifications include an `isInInitialList` flag to distinguish initial sync from live updates\\n- A ring buffer prevents slow handlers from blocking others\\n- Resync events periodically replay all cached objects to handlers that request them\\n\\n## Synchronization and Starting\\nThe `Start()` method in the factory (lines 143-165) initiates the entire pipeline:\\n1. Starts all registered informers in parallel goroutines\\n2. Each informer's Run() method starts its controller\\n3. The controller starts the reflector and begins the process loop\\n4. `WaitForCacheSync()` polls all informers' `HasSynced()` methods until they return true\\n5. Once synced, the local cache contains all objects from the API server\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that all components in Kubernetes that need to watch API resources can efficiently maintain a local cache in sync with the API server, with minimal network overhead and strong consistency guarantees.\"\n}\n",

Runs Reflector in a goroutine to feed the DeltaFIFO queue\\n3. `processLoop()` continuously pops items from the DeltaFIFO and processes them\\n4. `processDeltas()` updates the local cache and invokes registered handlers\\n\\n## Delta FIFO Queue\\nThe `DeltaFIFO` in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/delta_fifo.go` (lines 60-178) is the critical queue implementation:\\n- Tracks changes as `Deltas` - sequences of state changes (Added, Updated, Deleted, Sync, Replaced)\\n- Deduplicates consecutive identical operations\\n- Maintains FIFO ordering for processing\\n- Integrates with the local cache (\\\"knownObjects\\\") to generate synthetic Deleted deltas when objects disappear\\n- Supports periodic resync operations to detect missed updates\\n- Pop() operations are blocking, allowing the consumer to process one item at a time\\n\\n## Event Distribution\\nOnce items are processed by the controller and the local cache is updated, the `sharedProcessor` and `processorListener` components (in shared_informer.go, lines 705-991) distribute notifications to event handlers:\\n- Multiple event handlers can be registered on a single informer\\n- Handlers receive OnAdd, OnUpdate, OnDelete callbacks\\n- Notifications include an `isInInitialList` flag to distinguish initial sync from live updates\\n- A ring buffer prevents slow handlers from blocking others\\n- Resync events periodically replay all cached objects to handlers that request them\\n\\n## Synchronization and Starting\\nThe `Start()` method in the factory (lines 143-165) initiates the entire pipeline:\\n1. Starts all registered informers in parallel goroutines\\n2. Each informer's Run() method starts its controller\\n3. The controller starts the reflector and begins the process loop\\n4. `WaitForCacheSync()` polls all informers' `HasSynced()` methods until they return true\\n5. Once synced, the local cache contains all objects from the API server\\n\\nThis architecture ensures that all components in Kubernetes that need to watch API resources can efficiently maintain a local cache in sync with the API server, with minimal network overhead and strong consistency guarantees.\"\n}\n",
